01-02-2021 1128199612 Request Code Yara Release 8.9 WLC 8.9 28-02-2019 184739955 Request Code Source Code Offer To request a copy of source code that you may be entitled to receive under the applicable open source license(s) (such as the GNU L/GPL), please submit this form. Your request must relate to a product release that was distributed by Cisco within the past 3 years (or in the case of GPLv3 only, a product release for which Cisco still provides support and/or spare parts) and should include as much information as possible about the specific product or open source components you are interested in (including the reference number from the product’s open source documentation file if available). Requests that are missing information may take longer to process. For large requests or request covering multiple products, we may charge you a fee equal to the physical cost of providing you the source code. Cisco is a Leader in Open Source Innovation Open source is changing the technology industry and Cisco is a dedicated partner in that innovation. Cisco has been participating in open source development for nearly 3 decades, including founding projects like OpenDaylight, FD.io, VPP, PNDA, SNAS, and OpenH264, and contributing to projects like OPNFV, Kubernetes, OpenStack, Ansible, Chef, Puppet, Maven, and countless more. To put that in perspective, Cisco email addresses make an average of 1500 new contributions to Github every month. Cisco has also been a key contributor to the Linux kernel over the years, accounting for approximately 0.5% of total kernel commits, and is a Platinum Member of the Linux Foundation and Premium Sponsor of the Open Source Initiative. For more information on Cisco’s open source development and community participation, go to https://developer.cisco.com/site/opensource/. Recently, we joined RedHat, Facebook, Google, IBM, Microsoft, HPE, SAP, CA Technologies, and SUSE in making the following announcement with regards to our Linux (and other GPL-licensed) contributions: https://www.redhat.com/en/about/press-releases/momentum-builds-new-wave-technology-industry-leaders-join-efforts-increase-predictability-open-source-licensing. We believe this pledge will better motivate licensees to find and promptly fix compliance gaps, and if more contributors continue to join in, eventually we can remove a bug from the open source ecosystem that has left critical software like the Linux kernel vulnerable to the innovation-killing actions of copyright and patent NPEs. When people think that one licensing misstep can jeopardize their entire project or business, it does nothing but hinder innovation and chill the adoption of important technology. We see this commitment as a necessary step in the right direction. Our GPL Enforcement Commitment Before filing or continuing to prosecute any legal proceeding or claim (other than a Defensive Action) arising from termination of a Covered License, Cisco commits to extend to the person or entity (“you”) accused of violating the Covered License the following provisions regarding cure and reinstatement, taken from GPL version 3. As used here, the term ‘this License’ refers to the specific Covered License being enforced. However, if you cease all violation of this License, then your license from a particular copyright holder is reinstated (a) provisionally, unless and until the copyright holder explicitly and finally terminates your license, and (b) permanently, if the copyright holder fails to notify you of the violation by some reasonable means prior to 60 days after the cessation. Moreover, your license from a particular copyright holder is reinstated permanently if the copyright holder notifies you of the violation by some reasonable means, this is the first time you have received notice of violation of this License (for any work) from that copyright holder, and you cure the violation prior to 30 days after your receipt of the notice. Cisco intends this Commitment to be irrevocable, and binding and enforceable against Cisco and assignees of or successors to Cisco’s copyrights. Cisco may modify this Commitment by publishing a new edition on this page or a successor location. Definitions ‘Covered License’ means the GNU General Public License, version 2 (GPLv2), the GNU Lesser General Public License, version 2.1 (LGPLv2.1), or the GNU Library General Public License, version 2 (LGPLv2), all as published by the Free Software Foundation. ‘Defensive Action’ means a legal proceeding or claim that Cisco brings against you in response to a prior proceeding or claim initiated by you or your affiliate. ‘Cisco’ means Cisco Systems, Inc. and/or its affiliates.
